Introduction

Rule-service is a RESTful microservice for retrieve rules in json format and transform in Siddhi query

Overview

HTTP verbs

rule-service tries to adhere as closely as possible to standard HTTP and REST conventions in its use of HTTP verbs.

Verb

Usage

GET

Used to retrieve a resource

POST

Used to create a new resource

PATCH

Used to update an existing resource, including partial updates

PUT

Used to update an existing resource, full updates only

DELETE

Used to delete an existing resource

HTTP status codes

Rule-service tries to adhere as closely as possible to standard HTTP and REST conventions in its use of HTTP status codes.

Status code Usage

200 OK

Standard response for successful HTTP requests.

The actual response will depend on the request method used.

In a GET request, the response will contain an entity corresponding to the requested resource.

In a POST request, the response will contain an entity describing or containing the result of the action.

201 Created

The request has been fulfilled and resulted in a new resource being created.

204 No Content

The server successfully processed the request, but is not returning any content.

400 Bad Request

The server cannot or will not process the request due to something that is perceived to be a client error (e.g., malformed request syntax, invalid request message framing, or deceptive request routing).

404 Not Found

Resources

Rule

The Rule resource is used to create, modify and list cep rules.

Listing rules

A GET request lists all of the service’s rules.

Example request

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/ceprule' -i -H 'Accept: application/json'

Example response

Fetching rules

A GET request fetches a specific rule.

Example request

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/ceprule/xb182509135201620' -i -H 'Accept: application/json'

Example response

HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json;charset=UTF-8
Content-Length: 246

{
  "cepRuleId" : "xb182509135201620",
  "createdBy" : "xb182754",
  "createdDate" : null,
  "changedBy" : "xb182754",
  "changedDate" : null,
  "tool" : "openbus_br_zabbix_v4",
  "filters" : null,
  "childs" : null,
  "siddhi" : null
}

Creating rules

A POST request creates a new rule.

Example request

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/ceprule' -i -X POST -H 'Content-Type: application/json' -d '{
  "createdBy" : "xb182754",
  "changedBy" : "xb182754",
  "filters" : "[{condition=And, field=platform, value=Wintel, operator===}]",
  "cepRuleId" : "xb182509135201620",
  "tool" : "openbus_br_zabbix_v4"
}'

Example response

Unresolved directive in index.adoc - include::C:\pedrozatta\Json2SiddhiCEP\build\generated-snippets/create-rule/http-response.adoc[]

Updating rules

A PUT request updates an existing rule.

Example request

$ curl 'http://localhost:8080/ceprule/xb182509135201620' -i -X PUT -H 'Content-Type: application/json' -d '{
  "createdBy" : "xb182755",
  "changedBy" : "xb182755",
  "filters" : "[{condition=FIM, field=metric, value=system.dsk.utilization, operator=!=}]",
  "cepRuleId" : "xb182509135201621",
  "tool" : "openbus_br_zabbix_v5"
}'

Example response

HTTP/1.1 400 Bad Request
